Free Talk

"Kindness Extends to Livestock" 227

— Xu Maoyong

The Reuters news agency in Berlin reported on the 25th of last month: "Today, the authorities issued an order to protect mute animals, stipulating that anyone who abuses mute livestock will be sentenced to two years in prison; it is also prohibited to make them carry or transport work that is beyond their ability. At the same time, cats or foxes are not allowed to be used to train hunting dogs. As for the dissection of animals, it is in principle prohibited. However, public institutions are allowed to dissect animals to resolve doubts when exploring suspected scientific problems; however, civilians who perform dissections without a passport will be sentenced to more than six months in prison."

A friend of mine sighed after reading this cable: "Is it just that people in turmoil are not as good as dogs in peace? Within the same era and the same country, are people not as good as livestock?" He remembered Hitler's persecution of Jews and the suppression of dissidents. The Reuters report of Hitler's "kindness extends to livestock" was also done by Hitler. So, my friend's sigh was: "People should be reborn as livestock!"

But I don't think so. Because I know that it is not absolutely impossible for humans to receive equal treatment as livestock, as long as you can change your attitude as a human being, you don't necessarily have to be reborn as livestock. So, how should the attitude be changed? This can be known by looking closely at the above cable: change to "mute."

There is a saying in my hometown: "A mute eats Coptis chinensis, he can't tell of his suffering." It can be seen that if you are not mute, you will definitely tell of your suffering. But this is very wrong, because speaking out becomes a resistance to those who make you suffer, and this is wrong. As for livestock, they are born mute. Everyone feels very bitter when they are abused, but because they are mute, they can't speak out. Not speaking out means not saying anything, and not saying anything means they can be protected. Therefore, if you are born as a human being, you can avoid disaster if you can imitate a mute, or livestock, and be able to not speak.

But under Hitler's virtuous government, will Germans no longer eat beef, kill chickens and ducks, or drive dogs and horses? Not necessarily! I believe Hitler has never seen Mr. Feng Zikai's "Protecting Life Painting Collection" and been influenced by it. I believe that Germans will still eat meat, still use animal power, but the livestock will be especially fat, taste richer, and have greater strength.

Pulling and Hooking 228

— Huaiqiu

Treating "lower-class people" or "helping" to ingratiate oneself with "upper-class people" by implementing "pushing" and "kicking." This is a passive means and career, the purpose of which is simply to ingratiate oneself.

In order to climb into the "upper-class people's" class, to obtain the reputation of "upper-class people," and to seize the real benefits of a half-official position, it is necessary to implement the positive "pulling" and "hooking."

"Pushing" and "kicking" are clearing the way or being ordered to sweep; "pulling" and "hooking" are doing one's own work: standing firm step by step, climbing one step at a time.

"Upper-class people" will not see you, this "non-upper-class person," rising. Since you are determined to climb into that class, it is most important to watch the wind. Once the wind has been determined, you will turn the rudder with the wind, sailing with the wind. The wind, which is very spirited in front, will not turn its head to care about you, so you have to follow behind and shout: "Lord Wind, I am behind too!" At this time, you also have to "push" a few hands and "kick" a few feet to show that you are not completely incompetent. Once you happen to encounter it looking back, now is the opportunity. You have to run forward desperately, "hook" it tightly, and "pull" it tightly with both hands. If it likes to go east, you have to follow it and turn to the east; if it likes the west, you have to turn to the west... and you must always be careful: "hook" it tightly, "pull" it steadily, otherwise it will disappear in a flash, and all your efforts will be wasted. Once you have "hooked" it and "pulled" it, then slowly you also change your nature, your tail is gone, your spirit is changed, your spirit is clear and your bones are beautiful, and you also become a member of the "upper-class people."

In addition, there are two other kinds of "pulling" and "hooking": one is "pulling" and "hooking" a group of peers to fill my treasure seat. Once I have ascended the treasure seat, it doesn't matter if I kick them away with one foot; another is that the people on the treasure seat sometimes have to "pull" or "hook" some "lower-class people" to support the scene and join in the fun. The prosperity of Mount Tai's incense is due to this.

Stone Cart 229

— Zhou Lengjia

The weather is severely cold, and the streets are full of desolate sights. Withered yellow leaves fall from the roadside trees, covering the ground. Occasionally, a gust of wind blows through, carrying them in a circle on the ground, making a rustling sound, and then stopping, enduring the trampling of people's feet and wheels.

A dilapidated cart rumbles through the street, breaking the silent air that has occupied this street for a long time. The cart is piled full of bundles of stones, ready to be transported to the construction factory to build houses for the rich.

There are six laborers pulling the cart. Four are pulling in front, with four tow ropes hanging from the iron ring on the roof of the cart, each person bearing at least several hundred pounds of weight on their shoulders. Two are pushing in the back, occupying one side of the cart's pole. The pole is huge, and sometimes they have to carry it on their shoulders and backs.

"Hang yu! Hang yu!" This natural cry comes from their mouths. They groan. The breath they exhale turns into white lines in the cold air.

The road has already reached its end and is about to turn. But it is still far from the destination.

The sky is beginning to darken, and the air is filled with white mist. But they can't see it. The heavy pressure piled on their shoulders makes it impossible for them to look up.

"Hey! Old Wang, put some strength into it! Turning!" said one of the people pushing the pole in the back.

The called Old Wang subconsciously tightened the tow rope in his hand. He is an old man without a son. His wife died early, and he only has one daughter who works in a yarn factory, earning meager wages. For the sake of life, even though he is of old age, he has to come out to pull this heavy dilapidated cart.

The cart rumbled as it turned a corner at this moment.

A gust of wind carrying sand and dust rushed towards them head-on, and they all closed their eyes for a moment. The weather is really very cold, and some people in fur coats are still shivering, but they feel hot, and their hearts are also hot.

"Hey! Go to the right and pull the wheels onto the tram tracks. It's much easier to pull this way." The person pushing in the back instructed again.

In fact, there is no need for him to instruct. Almost all the people pulling the cart have this awareness, and the wheels rolled onto the tram tracks under this awareness.

The weight piled on their shoulders suddenly lightened, and they couldn't help but breathe a long sigh of relief. At the same time, rough words also erupted.

"Ha! Gu Cailang, I heard that your wife had another miscarriage, is that right?"

"How could it not be? Hey! Little Lu Zi, that appearance was really miserable!" As he spoke, Yuan Cailang's nose tingled, and tears almost didn't fall. His eyes blurred. He seemed to see his wife lying in bed, with two children crying beside her. This scene smashed the middle-aged man's heart.

The little Lu Zi pulling the tow rope next to him didn't say anything, but he was dissatisfied with his life. He dreamed of climbing up every day, but reality never gave him satisfaction. His heart was filled with ordinary sorrow.

"Ah! Ah!" A tram came from behind them, which made them all panic. They quickly gathered their strength to pull the wheels off the tracks. However, it is easy to pull them on, but difficult to pull them out. Even if the people pulling bent their heads to their feet, and the people pushing pushed their whole bodies against the pole, it was all useless.

The people on the tram were a little impatient. From the driver to the ticket seller to the passengers, they all cursed. No one sympathized with them, but there were only scoldings.

It wasn't until everyone was covered in sweat that they pulled the wheels off the tracks. The tram quickly drove past them, leaving no sympathy behind.

Now the road in front of them is still long, but the sky has completely darkened.

Small Notes from a Guest Window 230

— Shu San

Ceng Gong's "Jian Wen Lian" records: "Li Gong of Xiya was fond of jesting. When he was in government, junior scholars came to see him. The Duke said, 'Today, gentlemen, try to compose a couplet. The first line is: "The flowers in front of the court are just beginning to bloom."' Everyone smiled at its simplicity and pondered a response. Someone said, 'Nothing is better than replying with: "Your Excellency, Mr. Li."' Everyone laughed and dispersed." Furthermore, Jin Wuxiang's "Su Xiang Sui Bi" states: Ji Xiaolan, the Grand Academician, once said that any phrase in books could be made into a couplet. A guest offered, 'Only women and petty men are difficult to deal with.' The Duke replied, 'A widow sees a widower and desires to marry him.' Both couplets are extremely humorous."

Four

I acquired two editions of Li Rihua's "Wei Shui Xuan Diary." One is the complete edition published by Jiaye Hall, and the other is a selected pocket edition from the "Xiao Yuan Cong Shu." The "Jiaye Hall" edition contains a passage that reads:

"Twenty-sixth day (according to the calendar, it was the thirty-eighth year of the Wanli reign), cloudy. Visited Yu Bocheng's new residence. He said that Lu Wuguan's 'Record of Leaving Shu' is even more wonderful than the 'Record of Entering Shu.'"

That Fang Weng had a "Record of Leaving Shu" is something I only learned for the first time here. , , In the complete works of Dun Weng, there is no such text. Checking the "Research Book" and "Chronological Biography of Fang " of , it only records Fang Weng's years of leaving Shu, and does not mention this book. I think that since Fang Weng had already written "Record of Entering Shu," writing "Record of Leaving Shu" would be very difficult, and even if he did, it might not be better than the former record. What is said here is probably Yu Bocheng joking with Li Rihua, or it just refers to Fan Chengda's "Wu Chuan Lu." "Wu Chuan Lu" is "Record of Leaving Shu."

Five

Li Rihua was a student of Chen Meigong. This matter is seen in Rihua's diary:

"Twenty-third day (according to the calendar, it was the fortieth year of the Wanli reign). Invited Tang Zigong and Zhou Jianzhi, but they didn't come. Jianzhi is an old friend from my Huating days, the grandson of Zhou Caochuang. Caochuang is now seventy and old. He used to be fond of wine, relying on his wealth to be arrogant, and enjoyed flowers, stones, and secluded amusements. I visited Song when I was young. Later, Chen Meigong immersed himself in the Book of Poetry. Caochuang was a friend of Meigong, and they were close. Now, it has been thirty-one years since then, but Caochuang's eating and drinking have not declined, which is commendable."

And on the twentieth day of the eleventh month of the same year, the diary also records, "Two gentlemen, Chen Meigong came, originally admired books , extremely liked Wang Shuming's 'Autumn Mountains Thatched Cottage,' believing it to be on the 'Qing Bian Tu.' Also, in the book of Jian Heng's child, he wrote, 'He seems to gain the wisdom of nature without a teacher in Jia Youxi's paintings. However, from Zi , Shuming, Lazan, and Youwen, everything is present in his brushstrokes. Learning is so profound, how could he just be a tiger child of Nangu, he should be the reappearance of the Great and Small Generals Li.'" According to this, Meigong was not only Rihua's teacher, but also had frequent interactions later.

Two Brothers (47) 231

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

So he went out.

It was a clear day with no wind. People in the street looked cheerful. Merchants were going about their business, office workers were going to their offices, and young girls were walking to their shops. Some were singing softly, happy because of the weather. The boat to Trouville was already full of passengers. Pierre sat on the last bench. Thinking

He thought L:

"Was she uneasy when I asked about that portrait? Or was she just surprised? Did he lose it, or did he hide it? Does she know where it is, or doesn't she? If she hid it, what was the reason?"

So he kept thinking, inferring from one thing to another, and reached the following conclusion:

That portrait, the portrait of that friend, the portrait of the lover, was kept in the living room until one day the woman first noticed that her son resembled the portrait. Undoubtedly, for a long time, she had been worried that her son would resemble the portrait; later, she indeed found that her son looked like the portrait. When she saw the appearance of this resemblance, she knew that people would eventually see it too, so one night she took away this terrible little portrait, because she did not dare to destroy it at that time, so she hid it.

Ben Er now clearly remembered that the small portrait had disappeared long before they left Paris. He thought the portrait disappeared when Zhe'an started to grow a beard, because his beard suddenly made him look like the golden-haired young man smiling in her frame.

The movement of the departing ship disturbed and distracted his thoughts! He stood up and looked at the sea.

After the small steamer left the embankment, it turned to the left, whistling, panting, trembling, and speeding towards the distant shore that could be seen in the morning mist. Here and there, large fishing boats with red sails could be seen motionless on the flat sea, like large reefs protruding from the sea. And the Seine River, flowing from Rouen, separated two adjacent lands like a large arm of the sea.

In less than an hour, he arrived at the port of Trouville, because this was the time for sea bathing. Bi Ben Er walked towards the beach. From a distance, the beach looked like a long garden full of splendid flowers. On the wide yellow dunes, from the embankment to the black rocks, umbrellas of various colors, hats of various shapes, and clothes of various differences gathered in groups in front of the dressing rooms! Standing in rows along the waves, or scattered here and there, like huge bouquets scattered on an boundless pasture. And the chaotic voices, the voices of people near and far scattered in the brisk air, greetings, shouts of children being bathed, women's laughter, etc., all formed a constant gentle clamor, mixed in the insensible breeze, and breathed in together.

Pierre walked among these people! The more he felt like a stranger, the more he felt separated from them, the more lonely he felt, and the more immersed he was in his painful thoughts, as if someone had thrown him from the deck of a ship into the sea a hundred miles from the difficult coast. He brushed past them, unintentionally hearing a few words; unintentionally seeing men and women talking, women smiling at men.

Educational News from Other Regions

The Annual Meeting of the Second District Social Education Research Association of Jiangsu Concluded Yesterday, Passing Sixteen Proposals on Civil Education and Social Education, the Next Congress Will Be Held in Tangshan in October Next Year 232

(Nanjing, 2nd) The first annual meeting of the Second District Social Education Research Association of Jiangsu Province opened on the morning of the 1st. More than 40 members including Guo Zhitong and Tang Chengsi attended, as reported in the previous newspaper. At 7 pm that evening, in addition to Niu Dangshan's speech, the welcoming party of the Jingmin Education Center included variety shows, piano ensemble, pipa solo, huqin ensemble, and drama, as well as performances by the music research group of students from the Jingmin Museum's folk schools and the Popular Drama Society. The guests and hosts were extremely happy. Starting at 9 am on the 2nd, the meeting continued. Zhu Baoliang, the representative of the Jiangpu County Government, Wu Jinlou of Yongjian Museum, and others continued to arrive. Chairman Zhu Jianbai reported on the proposed cases, which were sorted and summarized by Sun Zhongwei, chairman of the review committee, and Huang Guifu, the recorder, and printed into a review report. However, it was discussed whether to first discuss the central issue this morning (those not studied yesterday) or to discuss the proposals first. Sun Zhongwei advocated discussing the proposals first, and if there were any proposals that could be included in the central research issue, they would not be discussed for the time being and would be jointly studied when the central research topic was discussed. The public agreed. The chairman then asked Sun to report on the main points of the review before starting the discussion. 1. Regarding public schools, (1) "Proposal to implement public education with public schools as the center" (proposed by the Provincial Tangshan Agricultural School Museum), measures (1) each place should consider the situation of villages and villages and divide the public school areas, (2) hire local leaders in the public school area and people who are enthusiastic about public welfare to organize the school board, (3) select villages with a large population and a suitable location to establish public schools, (4) organize cooperatives, township improvement associations, and all other implementations should start from the school. The resolution is to pass the original proposal and the original measures. (2) "Public education centers and farmers' education centers in various places must each run practical experimental public schools as models for local public schools (proposed by the third section of Lishui County). The resolution is to transfer to the discussion of the central research issue. (3) "How should the holding of public schools make it absolutely impossible to enroll students?" (Proposed by the Yihui Public Education Center) The resolution is to transfer to the discussion of the central research issue. (4) "How can the public literacy cards be made effective?" (Proposed by Yizheng Public Education Center) The resolution method is to set up literacy cards in thoroughfares, which can adopt the method of looking at pictures and following words, that is, simple pictures are attached below the text displayed on the cards. (5) "How should the general illiterate public be able to know the important domestic and foreign news and common knowledge of the day?" (Proposed by Yizheng Public Education Center) The resolution is that social education institutions in various counties can handle it at their discretion in accordance with the original method. (6) "Organize township improvement associations to promote local autonomy" (proposed by the Provincial Tangshan Agricultural Education Center) The resolution is to transfer to the discussion of the central research issue. (7) "Social education agency staff should earnestly contact local agencies and people in order to promote social education" (proposed by the third section of Lishui County). In addition, the Yizheng Public Education Center proposed how to enable the public to obtain a strong influence of civic education, which is incorporated into this case. The resolution is to request the Department of Education to issue an order to the county governments to transfer the subordinate agencies to cooperate in carrying out the work.

The Next Congress Will Be Held in Tangshan 233

(Nanjing, 2nd) The Second District Social Education Research Association of Jiangsu Province held a meeting on the 2nd. In addition to deciding on four cases related to public schools, two cases related to township improvement, three cases related to agricultural affairs and business improvement, and seven cases related to social education administration, the next conference will be convened by the Provincial Tangshan Agricultural Education Center in Tangshan in mid-October next year, with livelihood education as the central research issue, and an exhibition and lecture on livelihood education will be held.

Zhejiang Education Department Replaced the Directors of Education in Eight Counties, One Resigned, Two Were Newly Appointed, and Six Were Transferred, One Was Transferred to the Province to Wait for Appointment 234

(Hangzhou Communication) The Zhejiang Education Department recently decided to replace the directors of education in various counties due to unsuitable personnel, ineffective handling of affairs, or requests to resign. The post of Di Yisui Tangxi was transferred to He Tinghuai to take over. The post of Di Yisui Yongkang was transferred to Hong Shimo to take over. Cheng Jingrong was appointed to take over. Zheng Shuzheng of Xin Deng was transferred to the province to wait for appointment. Wang Tieqiu was appointed to take over the vacant position.

Overview of the Chinese College of the University of Paris (3) 235

(5) Funding When the Chinese College was founded, the Chinese government promised to subsidize 100,000 francs per year, and the French government subsidized 20,000 francs. However, after it was opened, the Chinese government did not pay a single penny. The college was able to survive for seven or eight years only by relying on the French government's donation. In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, the Boxer Indemnity issue was resolved, and various Chinese and French cultural institutions were able to share in the profits. The Chinese-French College also received 10,000 US dollars per year. Therefore, the college's budget was established. This year's accounts have not yet been settled. The following is a list of last year's income and expenditure to give a general overview.

(1) Income: 253,725.00 francs remaining from the Boxer Indemnity allocated by the French government, equivalent to 10,000 US dollars, 20,000.00 francs subsidized by the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs, 138,210.90 francs from last year's surplus, totaling 411,608.05 francs.

(2) Expenditure: 175,400.00 francs for salaries, 29,306.25 francs for office expenses, 47,824.10 francs for books, 50,318.00 francs for publication fees and inspection fees, totaling 302,848.35 francs, and 108,759.70 francs in storage.

In addition to the formal income listed above, in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs specially allocated 346,500 francs from the unspent Boxer Indemnity. The college used 200,000 of this money to purchase Mr. Bo Xihuo's books, and 146,500 to purchase Chinese books. In addition, the college also provides appropriate subsidies to poor students who are interested in learning, or helps with the printing fees of dissertations, etc. The amount ranges from 1,000 to 6,000 francs. Last year, nine people received this subsidy.

(6) Library In the 19th year of the Republic of China, the Chinese College obtained a fixed building within the University of Paris, with a lecture hall that can accommodate 100 people, a small classroom, a self-study room, and offices for the secretary and librarian. The books are displayed on the walls of the four corridors and various rooms.

Although the college's library was established not long ago, it has allocated 50,000 to 60,000 francs as regular expenses in the budget every year. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, it also received a large amount of special funds. Therefore, the collection of books is particularly rapid and rich. In the 19th year of the Republic of China, it already had 25,000 volumes. When the former representative Gao Shuyu, the minister to France, arrived in France, he also donated 4,000 volumes in the name of Chinese people. Mr. Bo Xihuo sold about 10,000 volumes. Last year, when Mr. Bo went to China, he purchased 20,000 tons of books for the college. The collection contains many treasures, such as the works of Chavanne, Legge, and Couvreur. The types of books are mostly literature, philosophy, history, and art. There are also many records of geography, customs, and ethnic groups in various provinces, counties, and foreign territories of our country, many of which are out of print. There is currently no one who has been properly organized. The director of the museum, Di Babiyuo, has limited knowledge of China and is unable to do the job. It is planned to ask Mr. Wu Kang to take charge of the museum's affairs in addition to teaching from next year. Mr. Wu's knowledge of Chinese and French is very profound and can be said to be a celebration of getting the right person. The museum is currently only open one day a week, which is quite a burden for general students. After being organized, it is expected that it will be more convenient for readers.

(7) Publications There are currently two types of publications from the Chinese College. One is the fourth volume of the "Selected Translations of the Great Tibetan Sutra," the posthumous work of Shawan, which will be printed soon. The other is the Tang Dynasty History translated by De Luoduo, which has now been published. It has now been decided to print two copies of the original manuscript of the "Secret History of Mongolia" in Leningrad using photographic methods, one copy to be stored in the college and one copy to be exchanged for books with China. This is a mutually beneficial method.

The overview of the Chinese College is roughly as described above. According to the college, although it has been established for 13 years, it did not have a fixed budget and complete its organization until after the 15th year of the Republic of China. Since then, it has gradually developed, the number of students has increased year by year, and publications have been gradually issued, showing a trend of increasing prosperity. This is due to the enthusiastic management of Mr. Ge Lanyan. In addition, Mr. Bo Xihuo is a major pillar of the college, and he has received a lot of spiritual help. He inherited the mantle of Shawan Gedi and became the leading figure in French sinology. Now that he is teaching there, it has greatly increased the college's honor and prestige. This is why the Chinese College of the University of Paris is highly regarded by sinologists in Europe and the United States. In the past 30 years, more and more Europeans have been studying our country's culture, but there are not many such large-scale research and transmission institutions. Our country urgently needs to give it practical help and guidance, so that the college can continue to develop, complete the mission of Sino-French cultural cooperation, and promote the development of Chinese civilization, which is also the blessing of our country. (The End)

Local News

The Municipal Education Bureau is Preparing for the Graduation Examination of Middle Schools, and the Primary School Examination Will No Longer Be Held 236

The Municipal Education Bureau has already distributed forms for the graduation examination of the first semester of the 22nd year of the city, ordering the schools to fill them out and start preparing. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education sent a telegram stating that the regulations for the graduation examination of primary and secondary school students have been revised, and the primary school examination will be temporarily exempted from re-examination, the examination committee will be abolished, and organizational regulations will be formulated separately. The graduation grades of each subject in the school account for 40% of the graduation examination grades in each subject. The official seals for question setting and printing must be strictly sealed, and the regulations will be followed from this semester. The Municipal Education Bureau is actively preparing in accordance with the telegram from the Ministry. The middle school graduation examination will be held this semester, and the primary school examination will no longer be held.

The Ministry of Education Orders the Municipal Education Bureau to Order Zhengfeng College of Arts to Improve Earnestly, and the Request to Add a Department of History and Geography Teacher Training Major is Not Approved 237

(Nanjing, 2nd) On the 2nd, the Ministry of Education ordered the Shanghai Education Bureau, the general idea is that the privately-owned Zhengfeng College of Arts was previously approved for establishment and ordered to improve various points on record. According to the inspection report, there has been no progress in the past year, the curriculum is still incomplete, the students' level is mediocre, there are too many absences, the teachers' salaries are low, the equipment is simple, and the students' admission qualifications are mostly unqualified. Combining the above points, according to Article 6 of the Regulations on Private Schools and the Central Rectification Order of Colleges of Arts and Law, it should be strictly banned. In order to facilitate the last opportunity for the school to improve, it is limited to this academic year, and the missing points must be improved quickly and earnestly. The Ministry will send personnel to inspect and report again, so as to be able to re-examine and seize it. The request to add a Department of History and Geography and a Teacher Training Major should not be discussed. Please forward it for compliance.

The Grand Occasion of the 32nd Anniversary Celebration of the Patriotic Girls' School 239

Yesterday (the 2nd), the Patriotic Girls' School on Jiangwan Road in this city celebrated its 32nd anniversary of establishment. It was also the initial completion of the restoration plan. Therefore, a commemorative meeting was held at 9 am that day. The grand occasion is recorded as follows:

(1) Commemorative Ceremony When the bell rang ten times, the school flag was raised high, and the heavy door was opened. The Boy Scouts were energetic and distributed to their posts. The Public Security Bureau was also notified to send police to the scene to maintain order together. Teachers, students, and guests were seated. At 10 o'clock, the meeting was reported to be opened. Principal Sun, the chairman, reported on the purpose of the meeting, saying that the school has a glorious history, and many graduates serve in the society. Unfortunately, it was destroyed by the January 28th Incident and suffered a major blow. In the past year, he has tried his best to restore it, and today's achievements are all due to the confidence when he moved back. What is the confidence? The Chinese nation will never perish. Then, Jiang Jianbai, the representative of the Education Bureau, gave a training speech, and then Cai Yuanpei, the director of the school, gave a speech, the general idea being that food, clothing, housing, and transportation are necessary for life, and so is school. Then, Chu Minyi, the director of the school, gave a speech, briefly saying that the evolution of the world is entirely based on the brain. People in our country have always divided mental and physical work into two things. In fact, physical workers must also use their brains. Therefore, practical mental work can encompass physical work. The value generated by mental work is unlimited. At present, women must diligently seek knowledge. In the future, if they promote education or raise children at home, the Chinese people's wisdom will be fully developed, and Mr. Sun Yat-sen's doctrine of saving the country can be achieved. Next, Jiang Zhuzhuang, the director of the school, gave a detailed account of the history of the founding of the Patriotic Girls' School. Then, Zhao Zhengping, the former president of the school, gave a speech, the general idea being that young people must love their alma mater so that it can move towards development. Again, Zhou Yangao, the wife of school alumnus Cai Yuanpei, and Jin Guangmei gave ten speeches, and the words were awakening. Then, the teachers' representatives and student representatives gave eulogies. After the ceremony, photos were taken and the meeting was adjourned.

(2) Exhibition of Achievements On this day, the school also displayed the daily homework, Chinese, English, mathematics, physics, labor, household affairs and other subjects completed in the past few months of this semester in the classrooms of each grade for guests to exhibit and criticize. The exhibits were dazzling, and the layout of each classroom was ingenious, forming a rhythm with each other, and there was a lot of static beauty.

(3) Sports Performance Starting at 2:30 pm, the school's sports department performed sports in the gym. Li Jiyuan was the chairman and Chen Fen was the leader. The programs performed were: 1) Walking, 2) Black Team Exercises, 3) Baton Exercises, 4) Chorus, 5) Yanqing Boxing, 6) Correction Exercises, 7) Jumping Box, 8) Bilking Dance, 9) Ribbing Exercises, 10) Piano Solo, 11) Erlang Boxing, 12) Towel Exercises, 13) Double Lifting, 14) Raf Tufta Taft Dance, 15) Hanging Exercises, 16) Tai Chi Boxing, 19) Pyramid, 18) Bamboo Standing Competition, the skills were extremely pure. Then, the Central National Martial Arts Museum joined in the performance. Zhang Zhijiang, the head of the museum, personally showed his skills. There were many programs, which cannot be listed completely. At one time, applause rang out.

(4) Students Automatically Console Construction Workers The school's new dormitories, Renzhai and Yizhai, are under construction. On the day of the school anniversary, the sounds of permission were endless. The students were grateful for the efforts of the workers, so they automatically launched a consolation campaign, collecting money to buy towels, food and other items, and sending representatives to the construction site to distribute them to the workers to show their condolences.

(5) Alumni Association Meeting The school originally had an organization of the Alumni Association, but because most of the alumni over the years were scattered in various ports, the address book was lost after the war, and communication was difficult, so the progress was slow. Yesterday, taking advantage of the commemorative meeting, the alumni in this city gathered to discuss and decided to start with the investigation and then restore the organization.

(6) Dinner and Entertainment In the evening, all the teachers and students of the school had dinner together, and educational films were shown for entertainment.

This move is entirely for social service and does not accept compensation. Please pay attention to all walks of life. Please send the mail to the Guanghua University Accounting Society.

Huasai's Irresistible Force Causes Unprecedented Crushing Defeat to Youyou: Group A Match 丨13-2丨 Chen Rong is Disorganized, Defenders Injured 246

Huasai's victory over Youyou was originally a possible event, but Youyou's loss of 2-13 was indeed unexpected. Huasai's lineup is getting stronger day by day. The close connection, the average talent, and the outstanding artistic skills of each player have not been seen in Shanghai's football scene for many years. Even Agal, who caused a stir last year, pales in comparison. Initially, Donghua's victory of 2-1 was due to the fact that, in terms of true football skills, Donghua was not as good. Moreover, at that time, Huasai had just arrived in Shanghai and had just unloaded its luggage. The current situation is even more different than before. However, Youyou's talent is also among the best in Shanghai's Chinese players. The reason for the defeat lies in the disorganization of the lineup. The whole team is for themselves and cannot connect, which is also a strange thing. Yesterday, the three or four thousand spectators in Yiyuan, in addition to disappointment, were all surprised.

Eventful First Half 247

After the start of the match, Huasai immediately launched a full-scale attack. Within five minutes, Jones scored a goal. Wang Shusen's obstruction was ineffective, and goalkeeper Tang Yongchun failed to catch the ball and slipped into the goal. After the center kick-off, Aqiao scored another goal without much back and forth. Youyou inevitably lost morale after conceding two goals in the shortest time. However, they tried their best to cheer up and did not slack off. Unfortunately, Wang Shusen suddenly reported a foot injury and had to leave the field, fighting with only ten players. As a result, the storm became more and more intense, becoming an eventful time. Huasai took advantage of the situation and plundered, as if entering an uninhabited area,浩浩荡荡，不可一世. After the center forward scored the third goal, Xi Qiaosheng committed a foul and was penalized with a twelve-yard penalty, which was missed. The ball bounced back from the goalpost. Afterwards, a free kick was awarded, and right inside forward Jones headed it in, making it 4-0. Seeing that the situation was not good, Youyou replaced Wang Shusen with Zhuang Shihong, and Chen Jiaqiu took over as a midfielder, stubbornly resisting and boosting morale, striving for a counterattack. Sun Jinshun received support from Jiaqiu and scored a goal. After that, Zhuang Shihong was penalized with another twelve-yard penalty, and Tang Yongchun successfully saved the day, turning danger into safety. In the first half, Huasai won 4-1.

The Situation is Even Worse in the Second Half 248

In the second half, Youyou became even more disorganized. Huasai's fierce general Maolin was transferred from the right wing to his original center forward position, and his momentum was particularly fierce. In addition, Youyou's midfielder was the biggest loophole, allowing the enemy to drive straight in and run rampant. Therefore, the front of the goal was densely populated with enemy traces, surrounded on all sides, truly a "stormy city, every bush and tree an enemy soldier." Within seven or eight minutes, Jones scored a goal. In desperation, Youyou Zhong Yongshen received the ball from Sun Jinshun and broke in single-handedly, scoring a goal. From then on, although Youyou launched several attacks, the enemy's defenses were deep and impenetrable. Huasai's momentum was still unabated, and the situation became one-sided, with eight more goals being scored in succession, resulting in a score of 13-2.

The Pegasus Cross-Country Team and the Huaguang Track and Field Team have jointly launched the "Fei Hua Cup" Open Cross-Country Race, earnestly inviting various teams to participate, fostering camaraderie, engaging in mutual learning, improving the performance of Chinese athletes, preparing for international competitions in the coming spring, avenging past defeats, and striving for national glory. It is now scheduled to take place at 3 PM this afternoon at Jiangwan Fudan University, departing from Xiangyin Road outside the university's main gate, passing through East Sports Association Road and West Sports Association Road, and returning. The total distance is about four miles, or approximately seven thousand meters, along a wide and smooth route, making it extremely convenient.

The vast and bustling Xiangyin Road will be transformed into a battleground for heroes. The Huaguang Track and Field Team, with Wang Zhenglin as its mainstay, supplemented by new heroes, can form a tripartite force with Jiangnan and Baihong. Although the Pegasus Cross-Country Team has a large number of members, the hopes for generals like Jin Zhongkang and Li Yagu may be difficult to fulfill, but several individuals like Yang Qingxie and Lan Shijie have relatively balanced strength and may achieve respectable results, following behind the Jiangnan teams. In terms of individuals, Jin Zhongkang and Wang Zhenglin are a pair of "comrades," each displaying ambition and possessing strength, making it difficult to determine the champion before the competition. Furthermore, Dong Shuzhao, Zhou Guangwu, Yang Qingxie, Zhen Xingpei, Li Yanxiang, and Lan Shijie are all renowned generals who cannot be ignored. The top few places in the future will likely be among these individuals. In addition to the large silver cup jointly donated by Pegasus and Huaguang as a prize for the team champion, the Jiangnan Sports Normal School is also offering a silver shield for the individual first place. It remains to be seen whose trophy it will become.

Essays

Desire and Madness 264

— Kang Tun

"It is difficult to fill the pit of desire," is a common saying based on human experience. From a pessimistic viewpoint, "rampant human desire" has led to the decline of social morals. From an optimistic viewpoint, it is precisely because of the relentless expansion of human desires that the bizarre and dazzling modern civilization, both materially and spiritually, has been created.

The expansion of appetite has led to the amassing of delicacies from land and sea; the unrestrainedness of carnal desire has propelled the palace of art; the expansion of the desire for power and leadership has shaped the unpredictable political landscape; the accumulation of the desire for wealth has led to the extreme form of capitalism; and the stimulation of the desire for knowledge and the fascination with fame have expanded the authority of science and the opening up of new realms and the invention of new things. ... Thus, the desires within humanity have become the engine of creation, and all human affairs have become its wheels and gears, leading to mass production.

To expand desire to the point of madness is seen as a very dangerous thing by those who hold a philosophy of self-preservation and prudence. However, the enactment of modern civilization seems to depend on the unrestrained expression of these madmen and their madness; examples are too numerous to count.

Consider Franklin, who explored the Arctic twice to prove his belief in the Northwest Passage. As a result, his body was forever buried in the snowy Arctic ice. However, his first map of the Arctic sea route became the blueprint for later explorers. Cook, in order to find the future continent behind the Pacific Ocean, braved the winds and waves in a small boat and discovered the east coast of Australia, illuminating Australian geography to the world. The elderly Professor Piccard ascended into the stratosphere several times, setting a record-breaking feat. In the past decade, British archaeologist Antero ignored his wife's divorce lawsuit after sixteen years of marriage in order to investigate the historical sites of the Mongolian desert. ... Are these examples not due to the stimulation of the desire for knowledge, manifesting as a crazed dedication?

If humanity simply followed the beaten path, perhaps we would still be living as cave dwellers. It is precisely because there are those intelligent and courageous pioneers who venture into the wilderness, towards the rivers, towards the oceans, towards the skies, that they become the pioneers of civilization, providing a path for the masses to seek their own interests. Without these crazy pioneers, the masses would have no benefits to gain." These words of Francis Younghusband, the president of the Royal Geographical Society of England, are worth emulating.

Anecdotes of Revolution in the Eastern Paradise 265

— Wu Xinpei

Penang Island in the South Seas, with its bright mountains, clear waters, beautiful scenery, and extraordinary products, has been under British rule for over a century. Through the efforts of excavating mountains, opening roads, and constructing, its beauty has been further enhanced. Therefore, Westerners have praised it as the "Eastern Paradise." When Sun Yat-sen was traveling for the revolution, he visited the island several times. Tanjong Beach and the Xin Guang Garden were important secret locations for planning the revolution, just like the Wan Qing Yuan in Singapore and the Jue Xing Garden in Perak. With heroic sentiments and remarkable events, there are many anecdotes. Here is one of them.

Two years before the founding of the Republic of China, the Qing government was in disarray and deteriorating. Uprisings were repeatedly thwarted, morale was low, and the people were depressed. The pro-Qing party in the South Seas, led by Tu Yongyi, used every opportunity to ridicule our party. Therefore, Wang Jingwei, Huang Fusheng, Chen Bijun, and Yu Peilun planned to take advantage of an opportunity to strike at the Regent Zai Feng in the depths of the Forbidden City, emulating the assassination attempt at Bolangsha, hoping to inspire the nation's spirit through their actions. However, they lacked the necessary funds and were unable to proceed. Chen Bijun discussed the matter with her mother, Madam Wei, who had long been a member of the Tongmenghui and a staunch believer in the Three Principles of the People. Madam Wei readily agreed and provided the necessary funds. Chen Bijun then secretly went to Beijing and established the Shouzhen Photo Studio as a base for transporting ammunition and manufacturing medicine. Unfortunately, their plan was exposed, and Wang Jingwei and Huang Fusheng were arrested, while Chen Bijun and Yu Peilun narrowly escaped. After getting out of danger, Chen Bijun returned to Penang Island with Hu Hanmin to plot their rescue. Sun Yat-sen happened to be in Penang at the time, so they convened a meeting at the Xin Guang Garden by the Tanjong Bungah beach to discuss the rescue. Hu Hanmin reported the details of their arrest, and when he mentioned that Wang Jingwei and Huang Fusheng had been sentenced to life imprisonment, he burst into tears and could not bear to look up. They immediately raised a thousand dollars and publicly elected Wu Shirong, Huang Jinqing, Hu Hanmin, and Chen Bijun to go to Singapore to raise more funds. They obtained another thousand dollars and took it to Hong Kong, where Li Zhongshi and others were in charge of contacting and arranging the rescue. While Hu Hanmin was weeping and his comrades were filled with grief and doing everything they could to rescue Wang Jingwei, Wang Jingwei was in prison in Beijing. According to the prison guards, Hu Hanmin had died in the Xin Hai Uprising on March 29th. Wang Jingwei cried bitterly and composed a poem:

"All my life I have been devoted to the revolution, I am glad that your wish has been fulfilled. But I pity the blood of two men, not flowing at the same time. Suddenly, I hate my remaining life, and I cherish my love for those who die after me. It is difficult to suppress the events of the past ten years, the tide rises to the top of my heart."

"Falling down, we meet for the first time, without words, our intentions have shifted. The strings and the leather are often worn interchangeably, and the glue and lacquer have never been separated. We carry food together in the morning when we are hungry, and we face each other at night when Han is exhausted. We share the joy of the cold season, and our affection is better than connected branches." "Every day I hear news from the Central Plains, and I cannot bear to hear it with a broken heart. My thoughts are futile and fleeting. Bats mourn the famous scholars, and mayflies sigh for the group. I remember gazing at the hometown together, and I am filled with sorrow for the countless clouds." He then heard that Hu Hanmin's death was not true, so he completed three poems and stopped writing. Soon after, the Wuchang Uprising succeeded, and Wang Jingwei and Huang Fusheng were spared from disaster. It is difficult for us to imagine the joy and comfort in the hearts of Wang Jingwei, Hu Hanmin, and the comrades in the party at that time.

Alas! When national disasters strike, the primary condition for resisting foreign aggression lies in sincere unity. However, sincere unity and collaboration have been loudly proclaimed by both the government and the public, but what do the facts show? May this anecdote serve as the highest standard for today.

Brief News: At the "Big World" of the French Concession on Rue Cardinal Mercier, the strange Mr. Smagan Belier, who has traveled to Shanghai from America, has recently been hired to erect a seventy-foot-tall electric pole in the square. Starting at 9 PM on December 2nd, this person will ascend to the top of the pole and live there, exposed to the wind and dew, for seventy-eight days and nights before descending. Food and drink will be delivered by people in shifts. People who want to talk to him can use the telephone installed on the pole for communication. If you want to meet him in person, you can also ascend to the top of the pole. This person had previously experimented in the American capital, lasting for seventy-four days and nights, which made him famous all over the world. This time in China, he has prepared 10,000 foreign dollars, which are deposited in the "Big World" to guarantee that this undertaking is not a deception. Therefore, after ascending to the top of the pole, if anyone sees him descending privately and then ascending again, the money will be given to them.

Three Words and Two Phrases

— Bai Laixuan

What is love? According to the answer given by physiologist Thomson at a lecture at the Oxford Summer School, love contains three elements: (1) physiological needs; (2) mutual emotional attraction; and (3) intellectual harmony in terms of reason, will, and thought. He also said: "Being in love is the highest point of life."

An American university professor once said a word about mate choice: "Don't marry a woman whose 100-meter race exceeds 13 seconds."

The new historian Van Loon said this: "If there is no art and entertainment in the world, it is like a nursery without laughter."

Random Talk About Cartoons 266

— Qian Yun writes and Wen Dongliang draws

Our People

Getting on the train is always like escaping a disaster, everyone competing to be first, no one willing to fall behind. If the people don't change, the stationmaster has no solution. "The net bag is worn out, the leather suitcase bumps the waist, and by the time you curse like a pig, it already hurts like hell!"

A young lady's canned food was scattered all over the place, in a pitiful state; however, there was trampling going on, and no one saw anything, stepping on the cans with their feet, their hearts set on getting on the train: the young man was said to be avoiding the suspicion of gender, and I had to comfort myself with my so-called "sweetheart" and lend a helping hand. A gentleman sitting in second class looked at me a few times and said in a low voice, "Trying to please the young lady, with bad intentions!" I have no defense!

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 267

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Desiring to Be Near, Yet Separating: Reminiscences in the Same Car; Half-Crying, Half-Laughing: Leaning on a Pillow, Sick in the Declining Autumn

Even if Ji Zhi had decided, I still had him in my heart, and I would definitely return to Haidian after staying in the city for a day or two, so he came to the long-distance bus station to wait for me. Things don't always happen so conveniently; he met me as soon as he arrived at the bus station. He must have come to the station several times. Looking at it this way, it is easy to imagine what he feels for me. Of course, I have a husband and cannot have outside intentions, but he put in so much effort to send me back to Haidian; perhaps he had something to say to me. I simply didn't give him a chance to say it, which is something I feel bad about. I don't know when he will be able to come to Haidian again. If he does come, I should be generous and say a few comforting words to him. However, this is a very big secret as a girl. Apart from thinking about it thoroughly myself, where can I talk about it with a second person? Since that day, a knot has been tied in my heart, and I feel very sorry for Gan Erye. At the same time, I also hear rumors that Gan Erye and his brothers are at odds, and losing his job was because he wanted to marry the eldest daughter of the Yang family. He swore that he would not return until he became rich and married Yang Guizhi. Now that Yang Guizhi has an owner, no matter how much money he has, he will not be able to marry her. Let's see if he comes back? Guizhi felt very uncomfortable hearing these words. She thought, I never thought that Gan Jizhi's feelings were so devoted, and he suffered such a great sacrifice for me. But what good did he get? But if he really suffered a sacrifice for me, he shouldn't have treated me with such a cold attitude at one time. Perhaps those outside rumors are false? Thinking this way, she secretly inquired many times, and the news became more and more real. Gan Jizhi really made a sacrifice for her. She thought that others had suffered such a great grievance, not only not getting any benefit from herself but also suffering her cold shoulder. (257)

A Record of Cherishing Autumn at Tianchi, Where My Footprints Have Reached 268

— Zhang Qianjiu

Tianchi Mountain is located in the southwest countryside of Suzhou. According to local records, it is called Hua Mountain because there is a pond on the top of the mountain, in which thousand-petal lotus flowers grow. Consuming them leads to ascension to immortality, hence the name Hua Mountain. At the summit of the mountain, there is a huge rock called Lotus Peak. It is also said that there is a stone drum on the mountain, which sounded during the reign of Emperor An of Jin, foretelling the rebellion of Sun En. It is further said that there is a pond halfway up the mountain, located on a steep cliff, horizontally immersed in the mountainside, spanning tens of feet, hence it is also known as Tianchi Mountain. Thus, the name Hua Mountain is no longer prominent.

Last week, when the autumn light was not yet old and the wind and sun were clear, my friend Ou Xia invited me to travel to Tianchi together. Ou Xia is good at climbing mountains and can take photographs. He recruited a boatman and prepared musical instruments, fruits, and bait, taking on the task single-handedly. Accompanying us were five beautiful women, named Ning, Yi, Ni, Lan, and Fen, with bright eyes, white teeth, delicate eyebrows, and vermilion lips, adding much color to the trip.

There are two paths from Suzhou to Tianchi: one is to disembark at Shanren Bridge, which takes longer by water but is closer to the mountain; the other is to disembark at Baima Stream, which is faster by boat but the mountain climb is slightly longer. To save time, we agreed to board the boat outside Changmen Gate, passing through Maple Bridge and the ancient Jin Bridge, arriving at Baima Stream after three hours. We disembarked from the iron boat, hired a guide, and headed towards Tianchi.

Soon, the mountain gradually rose higher. Climbing up the steps, we entered a stone archway. The guide said: "This is called Dongxia Cave." After entering the cave for only a few steps, there was a grand monument over ten feet tall, with three characters carved on it: "Tian Yi Ren." The characters were over a foot in size, in red, and their meaning was unknown. After clearing the weeds, we examined the seal inscription, which read: "Donation for the Reconstruction of Hejiu Ridge Monument." Circling upwards, we crossed another stone archway. The guide said: "This is Xihuan Cave." Emerging, we saw an ancient temple standing majestically against the mountain. Entering it, it was quiet and deserted. A Taoist priest sat quietly reading scriptures. When asked, he responded that this was the Puji Temple. Behind the temple, there was a stone with a poem inscribed by the famous Suzhou figure, Mr. Li Yinquan, which read: "Once, the King of Wu ascended this mountain to celebrate the Double Ninth Festival, hence the name of the ridge." Thus, I finally understood the origin of the name Hejiu Ridge. After a quick tour, we continued forward. The mountain became even higher, passing through ancient tombs, which were in a state of extreme disrepair. The grand monuments were broken in half, and the stone horses were separated. I wondered if those who had put so much effort into building them back then had ever anticipated the present state of affairs. Advancing further, the mountain path became narrower, and the mountain was even more dangerous. People walked among the bizarre rocks, calling out to each other, and climbed with great effort, leaving behind a snapshot of our climb, as it was not easy to reach the top.

Winding and turning, we reached Jujian Temple. In front of the temple, there was a stone house over ten feet high, with a stone-carved Buddha statue inside. The temple was very dilapidated in the past, but the current abbot has begun to rebuild it, changing its old appearance. The temple is located in the flat area in front of the mountain, with grotesque rocks surrounding it. The temple buildings extend to the left and right, and entering through a moon gate, the plaque reads "Deer Garden," with a couplet that reads: "Not Deer Garden, Not Home, Half an Acre of Sparse Fruit, Half an Acre of Flowers," which is delightful to recite. Walking along the corridor, there are three open halls where one can sit for a while. The buildings are newly built, and Mr. Li Yinquan has inscribed the plaque "Lotus Rock Piercing the Sky." In front of the hall, there is a thatched pavilion where one can enjoy tea, and next to the pavilion, there is a spring that gradually flows into a stone hole shaped like a begging bowl. Daoist Liaowuji wrote the three characters "Begging Bowl Spring," which are large enough to fill the entire space. Further flowing down, it is ejected from a stone dragon head. Jiang Zhaozhou of Xin'an praised it as "Tianchi's First Spring."

After resting for a while, we left the temple and ascended to the left. At this point, we were among the stone forest. What is the shape of the stones? They are strangely steep and dangerously odd and beautiful - that's somewhat can describe its very best. The road was also rugged and winding, making it even more difficult to walk. It became gradually more dangerous and harder the further we progressed. If one was not careful, their head would be crushed and their bones broken - especially the little ones. Before I and Ou Xia came, we heard that there have never been many people in ancient times who have climbed Lotus Peak, one because there is no path, and two because the mountain is dangerous. Moreover, today we are wearing leather shoes. But since we have already come, how can we not climb it? Therefore, we instructed the accompanying friends to wait on the mountainside, and I and Ou Xia used both hands and feet, climbing the rocks and grasping the grass, and used chalk to mark the path, recording the dangers and obstacles, and finally managed to climb to the Lotus Peak at the summit. The peak is a huge rock, as big as three houses. The two stones opposite it are slightly smaller. The two stones stand opposite each other, truly like a lotus flower spreading its petals. Standing and looking down, we only saw the rocks, and I am unable to describe all the said stones using anything beyond my inadequate writing. At that time, the mountain wind suddenly rose, blowing people to the point of falling, so we sat on the ground and slithered down, both our hands and feet were injured by thorns and brambles. Speaking of this to our companions, they were all amazed. Looking back at the top of the mountain, we were filled with attachment.

World Language Research Special Issue Confucius said: Today, the world, write the same script.

世界語的吏命丨與丨一個問題 294

— 公樸

Last time, this publication issued a special issue on Basic English to meet the needs of readers. At the same time, it was decided that from this issue, several special issues on Esperanto would be published, because the latter's history and scope, as well as its status in international linguistics, far exceed the former. Therefore, there are also more submissions. As for why we advocate the study of this international linguistics, it is because in recent years, Esperanto's position internationally has been steadily increasing, and there are more and more books and newspapers that use Esperanto to express opinions. The organization of Esperanto societies can be said to have spread throughout the world, especially in countries with oppressed and small ethnic groups. An Esperantist can freely travel to various countries, and everywhere they go they can meet good friends who treat them equally and without racial prejudice - comrades of Esperanto. Because the purpose of the creator of Esperanto is to break down one of the biggest obstacles to international communication - the barrier of language. We know that many, many misunderstandings and hatreds internationally are caused by language barriers. Because Esperanto's purpose is like this, genuine comrades who understand the true meaning of Esperanto, when they meet, do not have the various misunderstandings that commonly occur when two foreigners meet, and the various prejudices caused by different historical backgrounds of different ethnic groups.

Today, China is in the position of a semi-colonial and small ethnic group. We will not ask for liberation if we have not, but if we want to engage in resisting this current state of international oppression, if we want to implement Mr. Sun Yat-sen's words - unite with nations that treat us equally and with the weak and small ethnic groups around the world to fight together - then advocating the study of Esperanto can not only be an important tool for uniting, but can also increase the revolutionary consciousness of the Chinese people. We know that Esperanto is the most scientific and easiest to learn language today. In China, where the majority of people are illiterate, in addition to popularizing our country's applied writing, if we want to advocate that the Chinese people should still learn several foreign languages, then the reporter believes that we should first learn Esperanto, because no matter English, French, Russian, German, etc., they are all not as easy to learn as Esperanto. At the same time, in addition to working hard to eradicate illiteracy, we should at least encourage the Chinese people to learn a foreign language - especially Esperanto. With the tool of Esperanto, on the one hand, we can understand the international situation that is oppressing us, and on the other hand, we can consolidate the front of weak and small ethnic groups around the world to resist together.

However, the reporter wants to solemnly declare that although the above text vigorously promotes Esperanto, the reporter is still a layman when it comes to Esperanto. However, sympathizing with the creator of Esperanto's grand vision and being determined to learn this unique international language has been around for thirteen or fourteen years, not just since today. But precisely because I am a layman, now there is a question that I might as well take this opportunity to ask the advanced comrades who have already learned Esperanto and have submitted articles. This question is how to give people who have learned Esperanto sufficient opportunities to practice, so as not to become rusty and eventually completely forget it. The reporter recently met Mr. Wang Yunwu, who had studied Esperanto, and asked for his opinion on Esperanto. Mr. Wang said, my Esperanto is completely forgotten, because there are too few opportunities to practice, so he feels that a language must have sufficient practical opportunities, and these opportunities are best to be very natural. In other words, there are many, many people who understand Esperanto, and then learners can easily encounter opportunities to learn anytime, anywhere. If not, there is always the possibility of becoming rusty and forgetting. However, Mr. Wang's learning was many years ago, so what is the situation now? How to solve this problem, I hope Esperanto comrades will write articles to answer this in the next special issue.

世界語構造的優點 295

— 顧亦男女士

Since the 17th century, there have been hundreds of artificial international language proposals. Among these hundreds of proposals, only Esperanto, first created by Zamenhof, has obtained the unique status of an international language and has been developing indefinitely in practical use by the general public in various aspects around the world. The most important reason why Esperanto has been able to defeat all other international language proposals and be supported and used by the general public around the world is the advantages of Esperanto's own structure: simple, easy to learn, and suitable for application in any aspect.

There are a total of twenty-eight letters in Esperanto. Except for the five letters A, E, I, O, and U, which are vowels, the rest are consonants. Whether vowels or consonants, each letter has only one sound, and there are no exceptions such as long or short sounds. One sound is also only represented by one letter. This is the so-called "one letter, one sound; one sound, one letter," so Esperanto is the most ideal writing system in terms of pronunciation.

The stress in Esperanto single words, unlike in English, varies from word to word and is unpredictable. The stress in Esperanto single words is always on the second-to-last vowel, without exception. For example, the word Lumo (light) has two vowels, U and O, and its stress is on the second-to-last vowel, U, and never changes.

In Esperanto, nouns, verbs, adjectives, and adverbs all have fixed endings, unlike in other writing systems where they are elusive and vary from place to place. In Esperanto, the ending of a noun is O, the ending of a verb is I, the ending of an adjective is A, and the ending of an adverb is E: it can be understood at a glance.

In Esperanto, there are fixed endings to indicate plurals, unlike in English and other writing systems where there are many exceptions (such as the plural of Man is not Mans but Men). The plural ending in Esperanto is J, without exception. For example, "one book" is Libro, and more than one book is Libroj.

In other writing systems, especially German and French, every noun has a "gender." For example, in French, the word "Japan" (Japon) is masculine, and the word "China" (Chine) is feminine. There is no such irrational distinction of gender in Esperanto.

In Esperanto, the accusative case has a fixed ending, without exception. For example, if you say "John hits Peter," in Esperanto it would be JohanobatasPetron. Jobano is "John," batas is "hits," and Petro is "Peter." The N after oPetron is the accusative case ending. You can tell at a glance that the person being hit is Peter, not John. Because there is this accusative case ending, the order of words in an Esperanto sentence can be freely changed as needed without being misunderstood. For example, the sentence above can also be written as PetronbatasJohancoPetro. Because there is an accusative case ending after Petro, it is not misunderstood as "Peter hits John." This cannot be done in other writing systems.

There are a total of twelve numerals in Esperanto: "one" is unu, "two" is du, "three" is tri, "four" is kvar, "five" is kvin... "ten" is dek, "hundred" is cent, and "thousand" is mil. For example, "five thousand four hundred thirty-two" is simply kvinmilkvarcenttridekdu, exactly the same as Chinese. In English, "five" is frve and "ten" is ten, but "fifteen" is fifteen d, not tenfrve. "Fifty" is frfty, not fiveten. And French is even more stupid, they don't know how to say "eighty," they have to say "two forties." Esperanto has no such drawbacks: "fifteen" is dekkvin and "fifty" is kvindek, which is very simple and logical.

Prefixes and suffixes in Esperanto have very ingenious effects. For example, the word bona means "good." Simply add mal (a prefix meaning "opposite") and malbona becomes "bad." granda means "big" and malgranda means "small." Also, knabo is "boy." Just add in (a suffix indicating "feminine") and knabino becomes "girl." claboristo is "male worker" and laboristino is "female worker."

As long as it makes sense in terms of meaning, two or more words in Esperanto can be combined to form compound words. For example, the roots fer (iron) and voj (road) can be combined to form fervojo (railway). The roots oskrib (write) and tabl (table) can be combined to form skribtablo (writing desk). okvin (five), jar (year), and plan (plan) can be combined to form kvinjarplano (five-year plan).

Having understood the various advantages mentioned above, we can know that Esperanto's ability to defeat other international languages is by no means accidental. These advantages make Esperanto an extraordinarily regular, simple, and easy-to-learn language, and further guarantee its past, present, and future victory!

世界語專論世界語與中國 297

— 尚可鈞

Except for the "Northern Bear", the vast majority of people, whether in advanced or backward countries, are being harmed by the magic hand of economic panic, especially the masses of semi-colonial China, who are suffering even more under the oppression of imperialist privilege holders. However, at the same time, this oppression is also promoting the connection of the Chinese masses, who are trying hard to struggle out from under the stone slab.

Because the connection of the masses is so important, although in this world with developed transportation, imperialist privilege holders cannot cut off the mutual contact of the masses, they are always trying to prevent this connection. When they see that the masses in various parts of the world still have difficulty communicating in language, they are very happy. Language barriers simply mean that even if the masses in various places meet, they have no way to precisely discuss how to solve their own pressing problems.

However, the daydreams of all privilege holders were finally awakened by the real world. "Esperanto" (Esperanto) has after all defeated all the international language proposals of the utopianists and has won the unanimous support of the majority of people in the world.

But there are also people who think: "Esperanto" has nothing to do with China. The Chinese masses are overwhelmingly illiterate. They have no chance to even learn the national language, so how can they learn "Esperanto"? Therefore, we must wait until the Chinese masses have solved the problems of the nation and themselves before we can learn "Esperanto".

These words seem quite reasonable at first glance, but the people who advocate this are truly the so-called "knowing one thing, but not knowing the other". The masses are demanding a solution to the problems of the nation and themselves, and the masses will inevitably find a solution. But how to get a solution? In order to gain freedom and equality, the Chinese masses must, as Mr. Sun Yat-sen said, use various methods to "unite the nations of the world that treat us equally" and the countless brothers and sisters in the world who are suffering the same plight, to "fight together." And in this international "union", the international language "Esperanto" has a very great significance. "Esperanto" is by no means a pastime for the masses after they have been liberated. "Esperanto" is a necessary tool for the "common struggle" of the masses around the world. The Chinese masses, who are on the move, must undoubtedly learn to use this language tool! "Esperanto."

Naturally, after the masses have achieved their goals, "Esperanto" will advance toward its future at an astonishing pace. At that time, "Esperanto" will reach the most perfect and abundant state, becoming the only language of mankind in a great community society, because of the collective creation of the masses of the world.

基本英語一世界語的比較 298

— 施豫

(一) Comparison of Pronunciation

Esperanto pronunciation can be considered the most ideal and in line with phonetics. Because it uses one letter to represent one sound, and one sound is only represented by one letter. Therefore, each letter has its own sound, with no change. Learning the pronunciation of its twenty-eight letters will allow you to accurately read any Esperanto word, regardless of whether you have read it before. Its stress is also fixed, always on the second-to-last vowel.

English completely lacks this advantage. English pronunciation is one of the most difficult of all European languages. Its Basic English fully inherits its weaknesses, without improvement.

For example, the K sound in Esperanto is contained in four letters in Basic English, such as: C in Come, K in drink, Q in Qujte, and X in Erchange. Also, F and ph both sound F, and Gh sometimes also sounds F, such as Rough. S and C both sound S, and X also contains the S sound, and so on.

This is the use of different letters to represent the same sound. There are also instances of one letter representing several sounds, such as C in Circle, where the first sound is S and the second sound is K; S in Business, where the first S is pronounced Z and the last two S's are pronounced as one, and so on. A letter can also contain two sounds, such as X. Two letters combined can represent one sound, such as ph, and so on. There are even letters that are not pronounced, such as gh in Night and K and D in Knowledge, and so on. The above examples are only for consonants and are already numerous.

As for vowels, there are twelve pure vowels in English, and with diphthongs there are a total of twenty-one, in addition to triphthongs. So the confusion in their representation is even more severe than with consonants. For example, ai in Said is equal to E in end, O in not is equal to A in Was, but not equal to O in do, nor equal to O in No; OO in Good is equal to U in Puh, but not equal to OO in Food; A in Ball is equal to or in Form, but not equal to A in Back or A in Last; ou in Touch is equal to U in But, but not equal to ou in Out; U in But is also not equal to U in Pull; I in Fightr is equal to Y in My, but not equal to I in It; E in Me is equal to EE in Week and ea in Please, but not equal to E in Let, and so on.

In addition, the stress also varies from front to back and has no fixed position, which needs no further examples. So Basic English, like Standard English, requires a lot of time to memorize the spelling and stress in addition to memorizing the pronunciation and meaning of each new word. It is impossible to read a new word that has not been read before without consulting a dictionary or asking a teacher.

(二) Comparison of Grammar

Let's compare the second chapter of the "Basic English Grammar" with Esperanto.

(1) For plural nouns, add SO, but there are 7% formal exceptions and 6 types of spelling exceptions. Esperanto adds J without exception.

In 50% of the nouns, you can add endings to form four types of transformed words. In Esperanto, under the logical permission of meaning, any word root can be added with endings to form various parts of speech; or with prefixes and suffixes to form words with various new meanings.

(2) The comparative form of an adjective is to add More (comparative) or Most (superlative). However, some add er or est to the end of the word. In addition, there are two exceptions. Esperanto adds pll (comparative) or picj (superlative) uniformly.

When an adjective becomes a word, ly is added to the end of the word, but there are three types of exceptions. In Esperanto, in addition to basic non-ending adverbs, any word root can be added with the ending E to form an adverb.

(3) The singular of the present tense of a verb has a distinction between the first and second person and the third person, and there are four exceptions to the method of distinguishing them. The third person has a distinction between singular and plural, while the first and second persons do not, but there is still one exception. In Esperanto, there is neither a distinction in number nor a distinction in person, and the ending as is added uniformly after the word root.

The present tense and past tense of verbs are completely the same, some add a final syllable, some change one or two letters, and some completely drop a word. And its future tense changes to use the method of auxiliary verbs. Esperanto uses endings to indicate them uniformly, present as, past is, future os: absolutely no exceptions.

The human imperative of verbs uses the singular form of the first person, but there is still one exception. Esperanto has no exceptions, and uses the ending U uniformly.

The formation of participles also has no fixed method and varies completely from word to word. In Esperanto, the endings ant (present), int (past), and ont (future) are used uniformly.

(4) The comparative form of adverbs has five exceptions. In Esperanto, like dealing with adjectives, pli or plej are added uniformly.

(5) The accusative case of pronouns sometimes uses the original form of the nominative case, and sometimes changes it, depending on the word. The changes in the possessive case also have no fixed guidelines. The possessive cases of Esperanto pronouns all add the ending a, and the accusative cases all add the ending n, without exception.

(三) Comparison of Vocabulary

If a language only has eight hundred and fifty words, then its ease of learning is inherently credible. But people can forcibly reduce the number of words; but no one can pull the world of the twentieth century back to the primitive world of ancient times. Mr. Ogden can limit the types of fruits to only four, birds and beasts to nine, and insects to three in Basic English, but he cannot extinguish or exterminate the rest of the fruits, birds and beasts, and insects, or prohibit anyone from mentioning them.

Originally, the size of the vocabulary should be tailored to life.
